<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Photos_of_victims_in_Tuol_Sleng_prison_(2).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2723" data-file-width="3732" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Photos_of_victims_in_Tuol_Sleng_prison_%282%29.JPG/220px-Photos_of_victims_in_Tuol_Sleng_prison_%282%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Photos_of_victims_in_Tuol_Sleng_prison_%282%29.JPG/330px-Photos_of_victims_in_Tuol_Sleng_prison_%282%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Photos_of_victims_in_Tuol_Sleng_prison_%282%29.JPG/440px-Photos_of_victims_in_Tuol_Sleng_prison_%282%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Photos_of_victims_in_Tuol_Sleng_prison_(2).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rooms of the <a href="/wiki/Tuol_Sleng_Genocide_Museum" title="Tuol Sleng Genocide Museum">Tuol Sleng Genocide Museum</a> contain thousands of photos taken by the Khmer Rouge of their victims.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1168" data-file-width="1760" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg/220px-Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg/330px-Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg/440px-Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Skulls in the <a href="/wiki/Choeung_Ek" title="Choeung Ek">Choeung Ek</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Pol_Pot" title="Pol Pot">Pol Pot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ta_Mok" title="Ta Mok">Ta Mok</a> and other leaders, organized the mass killing of ideologically suspect groups. The total number of victims is estimated at 1.7 million <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodians</a> between 1975 and 1979, including deaths from slave labour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yale-CGP_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yale-CGP-123">[123]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 6 June 2003 the Cambodian government and the United Nations reached an agreement to set up the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extraordinary_Chambers_in_the_Courts_of_Cambodia" title="Extraordinary Chambers in the Courts of Cambodia">Extraordinary Chambers in the Courts of Cambodia</a> (ECCC) which would focus exclusively on crimes committed by the most senior <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> officials during the period of Khmer Rouge rule of 1975–1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The judges were sworn in early July 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KD-Time_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-KD-Time-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p><p>The genocide charges related to killings of Cambodia's <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_Cambodians" title="Vietnamese Cambodians">Vietnamese</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cham_people" title="Cham people">Cham</a> minorities, which is estimated to make up tens of thousand killings and possibly more<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Case-002_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Case-002-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup>
</p><p>The investigating judges were presented with the names of five possible suspects by the prosecution on 18 July 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KD-Time_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-KD-Time-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buncombe_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Buncombe-130">[130]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kang_Kek_Iew" title="Kang Kek Iew">Kang Kek Iew</a> was formally charged with a war crime and <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a> and detained by the Tribunal on 31 July 2007. He was indicted on charges of war crimes and crimes against humanity on 12 August 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap-munthit-2008-08-12_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap-munthit-2008-08-12-131">[131]</a></sup> His appeal against his conviction for war crimes and crimes against humanity was rejected on 3 February 2012, and he is serving a sentence of life imprisonment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nuon_Chea" title="Nuon Chea">Nuon Chea</a>, a former prime minister, who was indicted on charges of genocide, war crimes, crimes against humanity and several other crimes under Cambodian law on 15 September 2010. He was transferred into the custody of the ECCC on 19 September 2007. His trial started on 27 June 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Case-002_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-Case-002-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Case-002_closing-order_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Case-002_closing-order-133">[133]</a></sup> and ended on 7 August 2014, with a life sentence imposed for crimes against humanity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McKirdy2014_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-McKirdy2014-134">[134]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Khieu_Samphan" title="Khieu Samphan">Khieu Samphan</a>, a former head of state, who was indicted on charges of genocide, war crimes, crimes against humanity and several other crimes under Cambodian law on 15 September 2010. He was transferred into the custody of the ECCC on 19 September 2007. His trial began on 27 June 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Case-002_128-2"><a href="#cite_note-Case-002-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Case-002_closing-order_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-Case-002_closing-order-133">[133]</a></sup> and also ended on 7 August 2014, with a life sentence imposed for crimes against humanity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McKirdy2014_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-McKirdy2014-134">[134]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ieng_Sary" title="Ieng Sary">Ieng Sary</a>, a former foreign minister, who was indicted on charges of genocide, war crimes, crimes against humanity and several other crimes under Cambodian law on 15 September 2010. He was transferred into the custody of the ECCC on 12 November 2007. His trial started on 27 June 2011, and ended with his death on 14 March 2013. He was never convicted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Case-002_128-3"><a href="#cite_note-Case-002-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Case-002_closing-order_133-2"><a href="#cite_note-Case-002_closing-order-133">[133]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ieng_Thirith" title="Ieng Thirith">Ieng Thirith</a>, a former minister for social affairs and wife of Ieng Sary, who was indicted on charges of genocide, war crimes, crimes against humanity and several other crimes under Cambodian law on 15 September 2010. She was transferred into the custody of the ECCC on 12 November 2007. Proceedings against her were suspended pending a health evaluation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Case-002_closing-order_133-3"><a href="#cite_note-Case-002_closing-order-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup>  In September 2012, she was released from prison on account of advanced <a href="/wiki/Alzheimer%27s_disease" title="Alzheimer's disease">Alzheimer's disease</a>; she died on 22 August 2015 at the age of 83 from complications of the disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>There has been disagreement between some of the international jurists and the Cambodian government over whether any other people should be tried by the Tribunal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buncombe_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-Buncombe-130">[130]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_the_International_Criminal_Court">By the International Criminal Court</span></h3>
<p>Since 2002, the International Criminal Court can exercise its jurisdiction if national courts are unwilling or unable to investigate or prosecute genocide, thus being a "court of last resort," leaving the primary responsibility to exercise jurisdiction over alleged criminals to individual states. Due to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_and_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="United States and the International Criminal Court">United States concerns over the ICC</a>, the United States prefers to continue to use specially convened international tribunals for such investigations and potential prosecutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Darfur.2C_Sudan"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Darfur,_Sudan">Darfur, Sudan</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/War_in_Darfur" title="War in Darfur">War in Darfur</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="474" data-file-width="359" decoding="async" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg/170px-Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg/255px-Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg/340px-Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A mother with her sick baby at Abu Shouk IDP camp in <a href="/wiki/North_Darfur" title="North Darfur">North Darfur</a></div></div></div>
<p>There has been much debate over categorizing the situation in Darfur as genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The ongoing conflict in <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a>, Sudan, which started in 2003, was declared a "genocide" by <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">United States Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Colin_Powell" title="Colin Powell">Colin Powell</a> on 9 September 2004 in testimony before the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Foreign_Relations" title="United States Senate Committee on Foreign Relations">Senate Foreign Relations Committee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Since that time however, no other permanent member of the UN Security Council has done so. In fact, in January 2005, an International Commission of Inquiry on Darfur, authorized by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council_Resolution_1564" title="UN Security Council Resolution 1564">UN Security Council Resolution 1564</a> of 2004, issued a report to the Secretary-General stating that "the Government of Sudan has not pursued a policy of genocide."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un-org-January-25-2005_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-un-org-January-25-2005-140">[140]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the Commission cautioned that "The conclusion that no genocidal policy has been pursued and implemented in Darfur by the Government authorities, directly or through the militias under their control, should not be taken in any way as detracting from the gravity of the crimes perpetrated in that region. International offences such as the crimes against humanity and war crimes that have been committed in Darfur may be no less serious and heinous than genocide."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un-org-January-25-2005_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-un-org-January-25-2005-140">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2005, the Security Council formally referred the situation in Darfur to the Prosecutor of the International Criminal Court, taking into account the Commission report but without mentioning any specific crimes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> Two permanent members of the Security Council, the United States and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">China</a>, abstained from the vote on the referral resolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> As of his fourth report to the Security Council, the Prosecutor has found "reasonable grounds to believe that the individuals identified [in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council_Resolution_1593" title="UN Security Council Resolution 1593">UN Security Council Resolution 1593</a>] have committed crimes against humanity and war crimes," but did not find sufficient evidence to prosecute for genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2007, the Judges of the ICC issued arrest warrants against the former Minister of State for the Interior, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ahmad_Harun" title="Ahmad Harun">Ahmad Harun</a>, and a Militia <a href="/wiki/Janjaweed" title="Janjaweed">Janjaweed</a> leader, <a href="/wiki/Ali_Kushayb" title="Ali Kushayb">Ali Kushayb</a>, for crimes against humanity and war crimes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 July 2008, prosecutors at the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> (ICC), filed ten charges of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_crimes" title="War crimes">war crimes</a> against Sudan's President <a href="/wiki/Omar_al-Bashir" title="Omar al-Bashir">Omar al-Bashir</a>: three counts of genocide, five of <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a> and two of murder. The ICC's prosecutors claimed that al-Bashir "masterminded and implemented a plan to destroy in substantial part" three tribal groups in Darfur because of their ethnicity.
</p><p>On 4 March 2009, the ICC issued a warrant of arrest for Omar Al Bashir, President of Sudan as the ICC Pre-Trial Chamber I concluded that his position as head of state does not grant him immunity against prosecution before the ICC. The warrant was for war crimes and crimes against humanity. It did not include the crime of genocide because the majority of the Chamber did not find that the prosecutors had provided enough evidence to include such a charge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Later the decision was changed by the Appeals Panel and after issuing the second decision, charges against Omar al-Bashir include three counts of genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Examples">Examples</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Genocides_in_history" title="Genocides in history">Genocides in history</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a more comprehensive list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_genocides_by_death_toll" title="List of genocides by death toll">List of genocides by death toll</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208,_KZ_Mauthausen,_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="494" data-file-width="779" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208%2C_KZ_Mauthausen%2C_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208%2C_KZ_Mauthausen%2C_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208%2C_KZ_Mauthausen%2C_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208%2C_KZ_Mauthausen%2C_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208%2C_KZ_Mauthausen%2C_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208%2C_KZ_Mauthausen%2C_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208,_KZ_Mauthausen,_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Naked <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_mistreatment_of_Soviet_prisoners_of_war" title="German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war">Soviet POWs</a> held by the Nazis in <a href="/wiki/Mauthausen_concentration_camp" title="Mauthausen concentration camp">Mauthausen concentration camp</a>. Political scientist <a href="/wiki/Adam_Jones_(Canadian_scholar)" title="Adam Jones (Canadian scholar)">Adam Jones</a> wrote: "[T]he murder of at least 3.3 million Soviet POWs is one of the least-known of modern genocides; there is still no full-length book on the subject in English."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The concept of genocide can be applied to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historical" title="Historical">historical</a> events. The preamble of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CPPCG" title="CPPCG">CPPCG</a> states that "at all periods of history genocide has inflicted great losses on humanity." <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historical_revisionism_(negationism)" title="Historical revisionism (negationism)">Revisionist attempts</a> to challenge or affirm claims of genocide are illegal in some countries. Several European countries ban the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denial_of_the_Holocaust" title="Denial of the Holocaust">denial of the Holocaust</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denial_of_the_Armenian_genocide" title="Denial of the Armenian genocide">denial of the Armenian genocide</a>, while in Turkey referring to the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_genocide" title="Armenian genocide">Armenian genocide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_genocide" title="Greek genocide">Greek genocide</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Sayfo" title="Sayfo">Sayfo</a></i>, and to the period of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mass_starvation" title="Mass starvation">mass starvation</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_of_Mount_Lebanon" title="Great Famine of Mount Lebanon">Great Famine of Mount Lebanon</a> affecting <a href="/wiki/Maronites" title="Maronites">Maronites</a>, as genocides may be prosecuted under <a href="/wiki/Article_301_(Turkish_Penal_Code)" title="Article 301 (Turkish Penal Code)">Article 301</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup>
</p><p>Historian <a href="/wiki/William_Rubinstein" title="William Rubinstein">William Rubinstein</a> argues that the origin of 20th-century genocides can be traced back to the collapse of the elite structure and normal modes of government in parts of Europe following World War I, commenting:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The 'Age of Totalitarianism' included nearly all of the infamous examples of genocide in modern history, headed by the Jewish Holocaust, but also comprising the mass murders and purges of the Communist world, other mass killings carried out by Nazi Germany and its allies, and also the Armenian genocide of 1915. All these slaughters, it is argued here, had a common origin, the collapse of the elite structure and normal modes of government of much of central, eastern and southern Europe as a result of the First World War, without which surely neither Communism nor Fascism would have existed except in the minds of unknown agitators and crackpots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>According to Esther Brito, the way in which states commit genocide has evolved in the 21st century and genocidal campaigns have attempted to circumvent international systems designed to prevent, mitigate, and prosecute genocide by adjusting the duration, intensity, and methodology of the genocide. Brito states that modern genocides often happen on a much longer time scale than traditional ones - taking years or decades - and that instead of traditional methods of beatings and executions less directly fatal tactics are used but with the same effect. Brito described the contemporary plights of the <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_genocide" title="Rohingya genocide">Rohingya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_genocide" title="Uyghur genocide">Uyghurs</a> as examples of this newer form of genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The abuses against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Papuans" title="West Papuans">West Papuans</a> in Indonesia have also been described as a slow-motion <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papuan_Genocide" title="Papuan Genocide">genocide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Stages.2C_risk_factors.2C_and_prevention"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Stages,_risk_factors,_and_prevention">Stages, risk factors, and prevention</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ten_stages_of_genocide" title="Ten stages of genocide">Ten stages of genocide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Risk_factors_for_genocide" title="Risk factors for genocide">Risk factors for genocide</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Genocide_prevention" title="Genocide prevention">Genocide prevention</a></div>
<p>Study of the risk factors and prevention of genocide was underway before the 1982 <a href="/wiki/International_Conference_on_the_Holocaust_and_Genocide" title="International Conference on the Holocaust and Genocide">International Conference on the Holocaust and Genocide</a> during which multiple papers on the subject were presented.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> In 1996 <a href="/wiki/Gregory_Stanton" title="Gregory Stanton">Gregory Stanton</a>, the president of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genocide_Watch" title="Genocide Watch">Genocide Watch</a>, presented a briefing paper called "<a href="/wiki/Ten_stages_of_genocide" title="Ten stages of genocide">The 8 Stages of Genocide</a>" at the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">United States Department of State</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GSGW-1996_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-GSGW-1996-157">[157]</a></sup> In it he suggested that genocide develops in eight stages that are "predictable but not inexorable".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GSGW-1996_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-GSGW-1996-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Stanton paper was presented to the State Department, shortly after the Rwandan Genocide and much of its analysis are based on why that genocide occurred. The preventative measures suggested, given the briefing paper's original target audience, were those that the United States could implement directly or indirectly by using its influence on other governments.
</p><p>In April 2012, it was reported that Stanton would soon be officially adding two new stages, Discrimination and Persecution, to his original theory, which would make for a 10-stage theory of genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tbody><tr>
<th style="width:10%;">Stage
</th>
<th style="width:45%;">Characteristics
</th>
<th style="width:45%;">Preventive measures
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th>1.<br/>Classification
</th>
<td>People are divided into "us and them".
</td>
<td>"The main preventive measure at this early stage is to develop universalistic institutions that <a href="/wiki/Racial_integration" title="Racial integration">transcend</a>... divisions."
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>2.<br/>Symbolization
</th>
<td>"When combined with hatred, symbols may be forced upon unwilling members of pariah groups..."
</td>
<td>"To combat symbolization, hate symbols can be legally forbidden as can <a href="/wiki/Hate_speech" title="Hate speech">hate speech</a>".
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>3.
<p>Discrimination
</p>
</th>
<td>"Law or cultural power excludes groups from full civil rights: segregation or apartheid laws, denial of voting rights".
</td>
<td>"Pass and enforce laws prohibiting discrimination. Full citizenship and voting rights for all groups."
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>4.<br/><a href="/wiki/Dehumanization" title="Dehumanization">Dehumanization</a>
</th>
<td>"One group denies the humanity of the other group. Members of it are equated with animals, vermin, insects, or diseases."
</td>
<td>"Local and international leaders should condemn the use of hate speech and make it culturally unacceptable. Leaders who <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Incite_genocide" title="Incite genocide">incite genocide</a> should be banned from international travel and have their foreign finances frozen."
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>5.<br/>Organization
</th>
<td>"Genocide is always organized... Special army units or <a href="/wiki/Militia" title="Militia">militias</a> are often trained and armed..."
</td>
<td>"The U.N. should impose arms embargoes on governments and citizens of countries involved in <a href="/wiki/Genocidal_massacre" title="Genocidal massacre">genocidal massacres</a>, and create commissions to investigate violations"
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>6.<br/>Polarization
</th>
<td>"Hate groups broadcast polarizing propaganda..."
</td>
<td>"Prevention may mean security protection for moderate leaders or assistance to human rights groups...Coups d'état by extremists should be opposed by international sanctions."
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>7.<br/>Preparation
</th>
<td>"Victims are identified and separated out because of their ethnic or religious identity..."
</td>
<td>"At this stage, a Genocide Emergency must be declared. ..."
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>8.
<p>Persecution
</p>
</th>
<td>"Expropriation, forced displacement, ghettos, concentration camps".
</td>
<td>"Direct assistance to victim groups, targeted sanctions against persecutors, mobilization of humanitarian assistance or intervention, protection of refugees."
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>9.<br/>Extermination
</th>
<td>"It is 'extermination' to the killers because they do not believe their victims to be fully human".
</td>
<td>"At this stage, only rapid and overwhelming armed intervention can stop genocide. Real safe areas or refugee escape corridors should be established with heavily armed international protection."
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>10.<br/><a href="/wiki/Genocide_denial" title="Genocide denial">Denial</a>
</th>
<td>"The perpetrators... deny that they committed any crimes..."
</td>
<td>"The response to denial is punishment by an international tribunal or national courts"
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Other authors have focused on the structural conditions leading up to genocide and the psychological and social processes that create an evolution toward genocide. <a href="/wiki/Ervin_Staub" title="Ervin Staub">Ervin Staub</a> showed that economic deterioration and political confusion and disorganization were starting points of increasing discrimination and violence in many instances of genocides and mass killing. They lead to scapegoating a group and ideologies that identified that group as an enemy. A history of devaluation of the group that becomes the victim, past violence against the group that becomes the perpetrator leading to psychological wounds, <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarian</a> cultures and political systems, and the passivity of internal and external witnesses (bystanders) all contribute to the probability that the violence develops into genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> Intense conflict between groups that is unresolved, becomes intractable and violent can also lead to genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> In 2006, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dirk_Moses" title="Dirk Moses">Dirk Moses</a> criticised genocide studies due to its "rather poor record of ending genocide".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFTowner2011">Towner, Emil B. <li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFLang2005">Lang, Berel (2005). "The Evil in Genocide". <a class="external text" href="https://link.springer.com/chapter/10.1057/9780230554832_1" rel="nofollow"><i>Genocide and Human Rights: A Philosophical Guide</i></a>. Palgrave Macmillan UK. pp. 5–17. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1057%2F9780230554832_1" rel="nofollow">10.1057/9780230554832_1</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-230-55483-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-230-55483-2"><bdi>978-0-230-55483-2</bdi></a>. <q>On any ranking of crimes or atrocities, it would be difficult to name an act or event regarded as more heinous. Genocide arguably appears now as the most serious offense in humanity’s lengthy—and, we recognize, still growing—list of moral or legal violations.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=The+Evil+in+Genocide&amp;rft.btitle=Genocide+and+Human+Rights%3A+A+Philosophical+Guide&amp;rft.pages=5-17&amp;rft.pub=Palgrave+Macmillan+UK&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1057%2F9780230554832_1&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-230-55483-2&amp;rft.aulast=Lang&amp;rft.aufirst=Berel&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Flink.springer.com%2Fchapter%2F10.1057%2F9780230554832_1&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGenocide"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFGerlach2010"><a href="/wiki/Christian_Gerlach" title="Christian Gerlach">Gerlach, Christian</a> (2010). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=48N-XbOltMEC&amp;q=%22Genocide+is+an+action-oriented+model+designed+for%22&amp;pg=PA6" rel="nofollow"><i>Extremely Violent Societies: Mass Violence in the Twentieth-Century World</i></a>. Cambridge University Press. p. 6. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-139-49351-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-139-49351-2"><bdi>978-1-139-49351-2</bdi></a>. <q>Genocide is an action-oriented model designed for moral condemnation, prevention, intervention or punishment. In other words, genocide is a normative, action-oriented concept made for the political struggle, but in order to be operational it leads to simplification, with a focus on government policies.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Extremely+Violent+Societies%3A+Mass+Violence+in+the+Twentieth-Century+World&amp;rft.pages=6&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-139-49351-2&amp;rft.aulast=Gerlach&amp;rft.aufirst=Christian&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D48N-XbOltMEC%26q%3D%2522Genocide%2Bis%2Ban%2Baction-oriented%2Bmodel%2Bdesigned%2Bfor%2522%26pg%3DPA6&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGenocide"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFHollander2012"><a href="/wiki/Paul_Hollander" title="Paul Hollander">Hollander, Paul</a> (1 July 2012). "Perspectives on Norman Naimark's Stalin's Genocides". <i>Journal of Cold War Studies</i>. <b>14</b> (3): 149–189. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1162%2FJCWS_a_00250" rel="nofollow">10.1162/JCWS_a_00250</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:57560838" rel="nofollow">57560838</a>. <q>... genocide has become the yardstick, the gold standard for identifying and measuring political evil in our times. The label 'genocide' confers moral distinction on its victims and indisputable condemnation on its perpetrators.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+Cold+War+Studies&amp;rft.atitle=Perspectives+on+Norman+Naimark%27s+Stalin%27s+Genocides&amp;rft.volume=14&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.pages=149-189&amp;rft.date=2012-07-01&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1162%2FJCWS_a_00250&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A57560838%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft.aulast=Hollander&amp;rft.aufirst=Paul&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGenocide"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFGöçek2015"><a href="/wiki/Fatma_M%C3%BCge_G%C3%B6%C3%A7ek" title="Fatma Müge Göçek">Göçek, Fatma Müge</a> (2015). <a href="/wiki/Denial_of_Violence" title="Denial of Violence"><i>Denial of Violence: Ottoman Past, Turkish Present and Collective Violence Against the Armenians, 1789–2009</i></a>. Oxford University Press. pp. 18–19. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-933420-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-933420-9"><bdi>978-0-19-933420-9</bdi></a>. <q>The term 'genocide' is also contentious in that it has an inherent moral judgment, ... one that privileges the morality of the victims over the perpetrators.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Denial+of+Violence%3A+Ottoman+Past%2C+Turkish+Present+and+Collective+Violence+Against+the+Armenians%2C+1789%E2%80%932009&amp;rft.pages=18-19&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2015&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-19-933420-9&amp;rft.aulast=G%C3%B6%C3%A7ek&amp;rft.aufirst=Fatma+M%C3%BCge&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGenocide"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFIrvin-Erickson2017"><a href="/wiki/Douglas_Irvin-Erickson" title="Douglas Irvin-Erickson">Irvin-Erickson, Douglas</a> (2017). <i>Raphael Lemkin and the Concept of Genocide</i>. University of Pennsylvania Press. p. <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=kmw_DQAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA2" rel="nofollow">2</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8122-4864-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8122-4864-7"><bdi>978-0-8122-4864-7</bdi></a>. <q>In the late 1990s, the word 'genocide' began to be used as a type of moral category, taking on a symbolic quality as the crime of crimes, the darkest of humanity's inhumanity.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Raphael+Lemkin+and+the+Concept+of+Genocide&amp;rft.pages=2&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Pennsylvania+Press&amp;rft.date=2017&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8122-4864-7&amp;rft.aulast=Irvin-Erickson&amp;rft.aufirst=Douglas&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGenocide"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Platen_1831-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Platen_1831_15-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source" id="CITEREFGraf_von_Platen1831"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/August_Graf_von_Platen" title="August Graf von Platen">Graf von Platen, August</a> (1831). "Der künftige Held". <i>Polenlieder</i> (in German). <q>Die nur des Mords noch pflegen, und nicht der Schlacht, Des Völkermords!</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Der+k%C3%BCnftige+Held&amp;rft.btitle=Polenlieder&amp;rft.date=1831&amp;rft.aulast=Graf+von+Platen&amp;rft.aufirst=August&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGenocide"></span> (NB. Uses the term <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Völkermord</i></span> for the first time.<sup><a href="#CITEREFBöttcherBergerKrolopZimmermann1985">[A]</a></sup>)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Böttcher-Berger-Krolop-Zimmermann_1985-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Böttcher-Berger-Krolop-Zimmermann_1985_16-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source" id="CITEREFBöttcherBergerKrolopZimmermann1985">Böttcher, Kurt; Berger, Karl Heinz; Krolop, Kurt; Zimmermann, Christa, eds. (1985). <i>Geflügelte Worte</i> (in German) (4 ed.). Leipzig, Germany: <a href="/wiki/Edition_Leipzig" title="Edition Leipzig">Edition Leipzig</a>. p. 466.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Gefl%C3%BCgelte+Worte&amp;rft.place=Leipzig%2C+Germany&amp;rft.pages=466&amp;rft.edition=4&amp;rft.pub=Edition+Leipzig&amp;rft.date=1985&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGenocide"></span> (NB. The editors cite <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/August_Graf_von_Platen" title="August Graf von Platen">August Graf von Platen</a> to have used the term <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Völkermord</i></span> in his 1831 ode.<sup><a href="#CITEREFGraf_von_Platen1831">[B]</a></sup>)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation magazine cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source" id="CITEREFImhof1996">Imhof, Michael, ed. (September–October 1996). "Polen 1772 bis 1945". <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wochenschau" title="Wochenschau">Wochenschau</a></i> (in German). No. 5. Frankfurt am Main, Germany. pp. 177–193. p. 183: <q>Der letzte Act dieser Eroberung, die viel verschrieene Theilung Polens, war nicht, wie man sie genannt hat, ein Völkermord, sondern weiter nichts als die Proclamation eines bereits erfolgten Todes, nichts als die Bestattung einer längst in der Auflösung begriffenen Leiche, die nicht mehr geduldet werden durfte unter den Lebendigen.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Wochenschau&amp;rft.atitle=Polen+1772+bis+1945&amp;rft.issue=5&amp;rft.pages=177-193&amp;rft.date=1996-09%2F1996-10&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGenocide"></span> (NB. Imhof cites <a href="/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Wilhelm_Jordan" title="Carl Friedrich Wilhelm Jordan">Carl Friedrich Wilhelm Jordan</a> with having used the term <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Völkermord</i></span> in a discussion at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Paulskirche" title="Frankfurter Paulskirche">Frankfurter Paulskirche</a> on 24 July 1848.)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFTomaszewski2006"><a href="/wiki/Irene_Tomaszewski" title="Irene Tomaszewski">Tomaszewski, Irene</a> (2006). <a class="external text" href="https://www.google.com/books/edition/Inside_a_Gestapo_Prison/_kmRAwAAQBAJ?hl=en&amp;gbpv=1&amp;dq=Lemkin+ludob%C3%B3jstwo&amp;pg=PR13&amp;printsec=frontcover" rel="nofollow"><i>Inside a Gestapo Prison: The Letters of Krystyna Wituska, 1942–1944</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Wayne_State_University_Press" title="Wayne State University Press">Wayne State University Press</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8143-3887-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8143-3887-2"><bdi>978-0-8143-3887-2</bdi></a>. p. xiii: <q>In a letter dated October 3, 1943, Krystyna Wituska described the German atrocities in Poland … Wituska used the German word <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Volksmord</i></span>, in Polish <span title="Polish-language text"><i lang="pl">ludobojstwo</i></span>. Both words had been in use long before the war, and, while not endowed with the full meaning Lemkin was to give it, the meaning went beyond "mass murder." The root word, <span title="Polish-language text"><i lang="pl">lud</i></span>, can mean "people" but also "nation." In one angry passage, Wituska specifically wrote about Poles and Jews; it is clear she meant not just the murder of <i>many</i> people but the murder of <i>a</i> people.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Inside+a+Gestapo+Prison%3A+The+Letters+of+Krystyna+Wituska%2C+1942%E2%80%931944&amp;rft.pages=xiii&amp;rft.pub=Wayne+State+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8143-3887-2&amp;rft.aulast=Tomaszewski&amp;rft.aufirst=Irene&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.google.com%2Fbooks%2Fedition%2FInside_a_Gestapo_Prison%2F_kmRAwAAQBAJ%3Fhl%3Den%26gbpv%3D1%26dq%3DLemkin%2Bludob%25C3%25B3jstwo%26pg%3DPR13%26printsec%3Dfrontcover&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGenocide"></span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-ushmm-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-ushmm_22-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ushmm_22-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://www.ushmm.org/wlc/en/article.php?ModuleId=10007050" rel="nofollow">"Coining a Word and Championing a Cause: The Story of Raphael Lemkin"</a>. <i>ushmm.org</i>. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">22 October</span> 2017</span>. <q>Lemkin's memoirs detail early exposure to the history of Ottoman attacks against Armenians (which most scholars believe constitute genocide), antisemitic pogroms, and other histories of group-targeted violence as key to forming his beliefs about the need for legal protection of groups.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=ushmm.org&amp;rft.atitle=Coining+a+Word+and+Championing+a+Cause%3A+The+Story+of+Raphael+Lemkin&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ushmm.org%2Fwlc%2Fen%2Farticle.php%3FModuleId%3D10007050&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGenocide"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFSchabas2009"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_A._Schabas" title="William A. Schabas">Schabas, William A.</a> (2009). <i>Genocide in International Law: The Crime of Crimes</i> (2nd ed.). Cambridge: Cambridge University Press. p. 160. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780521719001" title="Special:BookSources/9780521719001"><bdi>9780521719001</bdi></a>. <q>Rigorous examination of the travaux fails to confirm a popular impression in the literature that the opposition to inclusion of political genocide was some Soviet machination. The Soviet views were also shared by a number of other States for whom it is difficult to establish any geographic or social common denominator: Lebanon, Sweden, Brazil, Peru, Venezuela, the Philippines, the Dominican Republic, Iran, Egypt, Belgium, and Uruguay. The exclusion of political groups was in fact originally promoted by a non-governmental organization, the World Jewish Congress, and it corresponded to Raphael Lemkin's vision of the nature of the crime of genocide.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Genocide+in+International+Law%3A+The+Crime+of+Crimes&amp;rft.place=Cambridge&amp;rft.pages=160&amp;rft.edition=2nd&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.isbn=9780521719001&amp;rft.aulast=Schabas&amp;rft.aufirst=William+A.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGenocide"></span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-111"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-111">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_Former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the Former Yugoslavia">International Criminal Tribunal for the Former Yugoslavia</a> found in <a class="external text" href="http://www.worldlii.org/int/cases/ICTY/2001/8.html" rel="nofollow">Prosecutor v. <li id="cite_note-114"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-114">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">ECHR <i>Jorgic v. Germany Judgment</i>, 12 July 2007. § 44 citing Prosecutor v. Kupreskic and Others (IT-95-16-T, judgment of 14 January 2000), § 751. On 14 January 2000, the ICTY ruled in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Prosecutor_v._Kupreskic_and_Others&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Prosecutor v. Kupreskic and Others (page does not exist)">Prosecutor v. Kupreskic and Others</a> case that the killing of 116 Muslims in order to expel the Muslim population from a village amounted to persecution, not genocide.</span>

<li id="cite_note-146"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-146">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.icc-cpi.int/CourtRecords/CR2010_04826.PDF" rel="nofollow">"Situation in Darfur, Sudan: <i>The Prosecutor v. Omar Hassan Ahmad Al Bashir</i>"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. International Criminal Court. 12 July 2010<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">28 August</span> 2021</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Situation+in+Darfur%2C+Sudan%3A+The+Prosecutor+v.+Omar+Hassan+Ahmad+Al+Bashir&amp;rft.pub=International+Criminal+Court&amp;rft.date=2010-07-12&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.icc-cpi.int%2FCourtRecords%2FCR2010_04826.PDF&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGenocide"></span><span class="cs1-maint citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Cite_web" title="Template:Cite web">cite web</a>}}</code>:  CS1 maint: url-status (<a href="/wiki/Category:CS1_maint:_url-status" title="Category:CS1 maint: url-status">link</a>)</span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-147"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-147">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFJones2017">Jones, Adam (2017). <i>Genocide: A Comprehensive Introduction</i> (3rd ed.). London: Routledge. p. 377. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781138823846" title="Special:BookSources/9781138823846"><bdi>9781138823846</bdi></a>. <q><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>Next to the Jews in Europe,' wrote <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Werth" title="Alexander Werth">Alexander Werth</a>', 'the biggest single German crime was undoubtedly the extermination by hunger, exposure and in other ways of ... Russian war prisoners.' Yet the murder of at least 3.3 million Soviet POWs is one of the least-known of modern genocides; there is still no full-length book on the subject in English. It also stands as one of the most intensive genocides of all time: 'a holocaust that devoured millions,' as <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Merridale" title="Catherine Merridale">Catherine Merridale</a> acknowledges. The large majority of POWs, some 2.8 million, were killed in just eight months of 1941–42, a rate of slaughter matched (to my knowledge) only by the 1994 Rwanda genocide.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Genocide%3A+A+Comprehensive+Introduction&amp;rft.place=London&amp;rft.pages=377&amp;rft.edition=3rd&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2017&amp;rft.isbn=9781138823846&amp;rft.aulast=Jones&amp;rft.aufirst=Adam&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGenocide"></span></span>
</li>
